<li>1380 AD: <a href="/wiki/Madhava_of_Sangamagrama" title="Madhava of Sangamagrama">Madhava of Sangamagrama</a> discovers the most precise estimate of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span> in the medieval world through his infinite series, a strict inequality with uncertainty 3e-13.</li>
<li>1480 AD: <a href="/wiki/Madhava_of_Sangamagrama" title="Madhava of Sangamagrama">Madhava of Sangamagrama</a> found pi and that it was infinite.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physics_4">Physics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Physics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomy_5">Astronomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Astronomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>1058 AD: <a href="/wiki/Al-Zarq%C4%81l%C4%AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Zarqālī">al-Zarqālī</a> in Islamic Spain discovers the apsidal precession of the sun.</li>
<li>c. 1500 AD: <a href="/wiki/Nilakantha_Somayaji" title="Nilakantha Somayaji">Nilakantha Somayaji</a> develops a model similar to the <a href="/wiki/Tychonic_system" title="Tychonic system">Tychonic system</a>. His model has been described as mathematically more efficient than the Tychonic system due to correctly considering the equation of the centre and <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudinal</a> motion of Mercury and Venus.<sup id="cite_ref-pcock_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcock-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mechanics_3">Mechanics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Mechanics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>12th century AD: Jewish polymath Baruch ben Malka in Iraq formulates a qualitative form of <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_second_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Newton&#39;s second law">Newton's second law</a> for constant forces.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Optics_4">Optics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Optics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>11th century: <a href="/wiki/Alhazen" class="mw-redirect" title="Alhazen">Alhazen</a> systematically studies optics and refraction, which would later be important in making the connection between geometric (ray) optics and wave theory.</li>
<li>11th century: <a href="/wiki/Shen_Kuo" title="Shen Kuo">Shen Kuo</a> discovers atmospheric refraction and provides the correct explanation of <a href="/wiki/Rainbow" title="Rainbow">rainbow</a> phenomenon</li>
<li>c1290 - <a href="/wiki/Glasses#Invention" title="Glasses">Eyeglasses</a> are invented in Northern Italy,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> possibly Pisa, demonstrating knowledge of human biology<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and optics, to offer bespoke works that compensate for an individual human disability.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomical_and_geospatial_measurements_4">Astronomical and geospatial measurements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Astronomical and geospatial measurements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>11th century: <a href="/wiki/Shen_Kuo" title="Shen Kuo">Shen Kuo</a> discovers the concepts of <a href="/wiki/True_north" title="True north">true north</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_declination" title="Magnetic declination">magnetic declination</a>.</li>
<li>11th century: <a href="/wiki/Shen_Kuo" title="Shen Kuo">Shen Kuo</a> develops the field of <a href="/wiki/Geomorphology" title="Geomorphology">geomorphology</a> and natural climate change.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_science_3">Social science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Social science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics_2">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>1295 AD: Scottish priest <a href="/wiki/Duns_Scotus" title="Duns Scotus">Duns Scotus</a> writes about the mutual beneficence of trade.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>14th century AD: French priest <a href="/wiki/Jean_Buridan" title="Jean Buridan">Jean Buridan</a> provides a basic explanation of the price system.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philosophy_of_science">Philosophy of science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Philosophy of science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>1220s - <a href="/wiki/Robert_Grosseteste#Science" title="Robert Grosseteste">Robert Grosseteste</a> writes on optics, and the production of lenses, while asserting models should be developed from observations, and predictions of those models verified through observation, in a precursor to the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific method</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RG_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RG-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1267 - <a href="/wiki/Roger_Bacon" title="Roger Bacon">Roger Bacon</a> publishes his <a href="/wiki/Opus_Majus" title="Opus Majus">Opus Majus</a>, compiling translated Classical Greek, and Arabic works on mathematics, optics, and alchemy into a volume, and details his methods for evaluating the theories, particularly those of Ptolemy's 2nd century <a href="/wiki/Optics_(Ptolemy)" title="Optics (Ptolemy)">Optics</a>, and his findings on the production of lenses, asserting  “<i>theories supplied by reason should be verified by sensory data, aided by instruments, and corroborated by trustworthy witnesses</i>", in a precursor to the peer reviewed scientific method.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_century">16th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: 16th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">Scientific Revolution</a> occurs in Europe around this period, greatly accelerating the progress of science and contributing to the rationalization of the natural sciences. 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematics_7">Mathematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Mathematics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Numbers.2C_measurement_and_arithmetic_5"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbers,_measurement_and_arithmetic_5">Numbers, measurement and arithmetic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Numbers, measurement and arithmetic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>1545: Gerolamo Cardano discovers <a href="/wiki/Complex_numbers" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex numbers">complex numbers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1572: <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Bombelli" title="Rafael Bombelli">Rafael Bombelli</a> provides rules for <a href="/wiki/Complex_arithmetic" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex arithmetic">complex arithmetic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Algebra_6">Algebra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Algebra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>c. 1500: <a href="/wiki/Scipione_del_Ferro" title="Scipione del Ferro">Scipione del Ferro</a> solves the special cubic equation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x^{3}=px+q}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>3</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>p</mi>
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mo>+</mo>
        <mi>q</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{3}=px+q}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/173fcb10c6cebd708d665a8e0e2ecf26ea5863e8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.891ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="x^3 = px + q"/></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>16th century: <a href="/wiki/Gerolamo_Cardano" title="Gerolamo Cardano">Gerolamo Cardano</a> solves the general cubic equation (by reducing them to the case with zero quadratic term).</li>
<li>16th century: <a href="/wiki/Lodovico_Ferrari" title="Lodovico Ferrari">Lodovico Ferrari</a> solves the general quartic equation (by reducing it to the case with zero quartic term).</li>
<li>16th century: <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Vi%C3%A8te" title="François Viète">François Viète</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Vieta%27s_formulas" title="Vieta&#39;s formulas">Vieta's formulas</a>.</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Probability_and_statistics">Probability and statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Probability and statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>1564: <a href="/wiki/Gerolamo_Cardano" title="Gerolamo Cardano">Gerolamo Cardano</a> is the first to produce a systematic treatment of probability.<sup id="cite_ref-Westfall_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Westfall-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Numerical_mathematics_and_algorithms_6">Numerical mathematics and algorithms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=86" title="Edit section: Numerical mathematics and algorithms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>16th century: <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Vi%C3%A8te" title="François Viète">François Viète</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%A8te%27s_formula" title="Viète&#39;s formula">Viète's formula</a> for <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-beckmann_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beckmann-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Notation_and_conventions_4">Notation and conventions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=87" title="Edit section: Notation and conventions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Various pieces of modern symbolic notation were introduced in this period, notably: 
</p>
<ul><li>1556: <a href="/wiki/Niccol%C3%B2_Tartaglia" class="mw-redirect" title="Niccolò Tartaglia">Niccolò Tartaglia</a> introduces parenthesis.</li>
<li>1557: <a href="/wiki/Robert_Recorde" title="Robert Recorde">Robert Recorde</a> introduces the equal sign.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1591: <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Vi%C3%A8te" title="François Viète">François Viète</a>'s <a href="/wiki/New_algebra" class="mw-redirect" title="New algebra">New algebra</a> shows the modern notational algebraic manipulation.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physics_5">Physics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=88" title="Edit section: Physics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomy_6">Astronomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=89" title="Edit section: Astronomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>1543: <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Nicolaus Copernicus</a> develops a <a href="/wiki/Heliocentrism" title="Heliocentrism">heliocentric model</a>, rejecting Aristotle's earth-centric view, would be the first quantitative heliocentric model in history.</li>
<li>Late 16th century: <a href="/wiki/Tycho_Brahe" title="Tycho Brahe">Tycho Brahe</a> proves that comets are astronomical (and not atmospheric) phenomena.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biology_and_anatomy_4">Biology and anatomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=90" title="Edit section: Biology and anatomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>1543 – <a href="/wiki/Vesalius" class="mw-redirect" title="Vesalius">Vesalius</a>: pioneering research into human anatomy</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_science_4">Social science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=91" title="Edit section: Social science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics_3">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=92" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>1517: Nicolaus Copernicus develops the quantity theory of money and states the earliest known form of <a href="/wiki/Gresham%27s_law" title="Gresham&#39;s law">Gresham's law</a>: ("Bad money drowns out good").<sup id="cite_ref-Volckart_1997_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volckart_1997-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="17th_century">17th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=93" title="Edit section: 17th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1600 – <a href="/wiki/William_Gilbert_(astronomer)" class="mw-redirect" title="William Gilbert (astronomer)">William Gilbert</a>: <a href="/wiki/Earth%27s_magnetic_field" title="Earth&#39;s magnetic field">Earth's magnetic field</a></li>
<li>1608 – Earliest record of an <a href="/wiki/Optical_telescope" title="Optical telescope">optical telescope</a></li>
<li>1609 – <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a>: first two <a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion" title="Kepler&#39;s laws of planetary motion">laws of planetary motion</a></li>
<li>1610 – <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Sidereus_Nuncius" title="Sidereus Nuncius">Sidereus Nuncius</a></i>: telescopic observations</li>
<li>1614 – <a href="/wiki/John_Napier" title="John Napier">John Napier</a>: use of <a href="/wiki/Logarithm" title="Logarithm">logarithms</a> for calculation<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1619 – <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a>: third <a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion" title="Kepler&#39;s laws of planetary motion">law of planetary motion</a></li>
<li>1620 – Appearance of the first <a href="/wiki/Optical_microscope#Compound_microscope" title="Optical microscope">compound microscopes</a> in Europe</li>
<li>1628 – <a href="/wiki/Willebrord_Snellius" title="Willebrord Snellius">Willebrord Snellius</a>: the law of refraction also known as <a href="/wiki/Snell%27s_law" title="Snell&#39;s law">Snell's law</a></li>
<li>1628 – <a href="/wiki/William_Harvey" title="William Harvey">William Harvey</a>: <a href="/wiki/Blood_circulation" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood circulation">blood circulation</a></li>
<li>1638 – <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a>: laws of falling bodies</li>
<li>1643 – <a href="/wiki/Evangelista_Torricelli" title="Evangelista Torricelli">Evangelista Torricelli</a> invents the mercury <a href="/wiki/Barometer" title="Barometer">barometer</a></li>
<li>1662 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Boyle" title="Robert Boyle">Robert Boyle</a>: <a href="/wiki/Boyle%27s_law" title="Boyle&#39;s law">Boyle's law</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">ideal gases</a></li>
<li>1665 – <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_Transactions_of_the_Royal_Society" title="Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society">Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society</a>: first <a href="/wiki/Peer_review" title="Peer review">peer reviewed</a> scientific journal published.</li>
<li>1665 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hooke" title="Robert Hooke">Robert Hooke</a>: discovers the <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cell</a></li>
<li>1668 – <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Redi" title="Francesco Redi">Francesco Redi</a>: disproved idea of <a href="/wiki/Spontaneous_generation" title="Spontaneous generation">spontaneous generation</a></li>
<li>1669 – <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Steno" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas Steno">Nicholas Steno</a>: proposes that <a href="/wiki/Fossils" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossils">fossils</a> are organic remains embedded in layers of sediment, basis of <a href="/wiki/Stratigraphy" title="Stratigraphy">stratigraphy</a></li>
<li>1669 – <a href="/wiki/Jan_Swammerdam" title="Jan Swammerdam">Jan Swammerdam</a>: <a href="/wiki/Epigenetics" title="Epigenetics">epigenesis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Insects" class="mw-redirect" title="Insects">insects</a></li>
<li>1672 – <a href="/wiki/Sir_Isaac_Newton" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Isaac Newton">Sir Isaac Newton</a>: discovers that white <a href="/wiki/Light" title="Light">light</a> is a mixture of distinct coloured <a href="/wiki/Ray_(optics)" title="Ray (optics)">rays</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Spectrum" title="Spectrum">spectrum</a>)</li>
<li>1673 – <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens" title="Christiaan Huygens">Christiaan Huygens</a>: first study of oscillating system and design of pendulum clocks</li>
<li>1675 – <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Wilhelm_Leibniz" title="Gottfried Wilhelm Leibniz">Leibniz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Newton</a>: <a href="/wiki/Infinitesimal_calculus" class="mw-redirect" title="Infinitesimal calculus">infinitesimal calculus</a></li>
<li>1675 – <a href="/wiki/Anton_van_Leeuwenhoek" class="mw-redirect" title="Anton van Leeuwenhoek">Anton van Leeuwenhoek</a>: observes <a href="/wiki/Microorganisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Microorganisms">microorganisms</a> using a refined <a href="/wiki/Optical_microscope#Types" title="Optical microscope">simple microscope</a></li>
<li>1676 – <a href="/wiki/Ole_R%C3%B8mer" title="Ole Rømer">Ole Rømer</a>:  first measurement of the <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a></li>
<li>1687 – <a href="/wiki/Sir_Isaac_Newton" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Isaac Newton">Sir Isaac Newton</a>: classical mathematical description of the <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundamental force">fundamental force</a> of <a href="/wiki/Universal_gravitation" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal gravitation">universal gravitation</a> and the three physical <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion" title="Newton&#39;s laws of motion">laws of motion</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=94" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1735 – <a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">Carl Linnaeus</a> described a new system for classifying plants in <a href="/wiki/Systema_Naturae" title="Systema Naturae">Systema Naturae</a></li>
<li>1745 – <a href="/wiki/Ewald_J%C3%BCrgen_Georg_von_Kleist" class="mw-redirect" title="Ewald Jürgen Georg von Kleist">Ewald Jürgen Georg von Kleist</a> first capacitor, the <a href="/wiki/Leyden_jar" title="Leyden jar">Leyden jar</a></li>
<li>1749–1789 - <a href="/wiki/Georges-Louis_Leclerc,_Comte_de_Buffon" title="Georges-Louis Leclerc, Comte de Buffon">Buffon</a> wrote <a href="/wiki/Histoire_naturelle" class="mw-redirect" title="Histoire naturelle">Histoire naturelle</a></li>
<li>1750 – <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Black" title="Joseph Black">Joseph Black</a>: describes <a href="/wiki/Latent_heat" title="Latent heat">latent heat</a></li>
<li>1751 – <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a>: <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> is <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electrical</a></li>
<li>1755 – <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">Immanuel Kant</a>: Gaseous Hypothesis in <a href="/wiki/Universal_Natural_History_and_Theory_of_Heaven" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Natural History and Theory of Heaven">Universal Natural History and Theory of Heaven</a></li>
<li>1761 – <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a>: discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Venus" title="Atmosphere of Venus">atmosphere of Venus</a></li>
<li>1763 – <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bayes" title="Thomas Bayes">Thomas Bayes</a>: publishes the first version of <a href="/wiki/Bayes%27_theorem" title="Bayes&#39; theorem">Bayes' theorem</a>, paving the way for <a href="/wiki/Bayesian_probability" title="Bayesian probability">Bayesian probability</a></li>
<li>1771 – <a href="/wiki/Charles_Messier" title="Charles Messier">Charles Messier</a>: publishes catalogue of astronomical objects (<i><a href="/wiki/Messier_Objects" class="mw-redirect" title="Messier Objects">Messier Objects</a></i>) now known to include galaxies, star clusters, and nebulae.</li>
<li>1778 – <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Lavoisier" title="Antoine Lavoisier">Antoine Lavoisier</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Priestley" title="Joseph Priestley">Joseph Priestley</a>): discovery of oxygen leading to end of <a href="/wiki/Phlogiston_theory" title="Phlogiston theory">Phlogiston theory</a></li>
<li>1781 – <a href="/wiki/William_Herschel" title="William Herschel">William Herschel</a> announces discovery of <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a>, expanding the known boundaries of the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a> for the first time in modern history</li>
<li>1785 – <a href="/wiki/William_Withering" title="William Withering">William Withering</a>: publishes the first definitive account of the use of foxglove (<a href="/wiki/Digitalis" title="Digitalis">digitalis</a>) for treating <a href="/wiki/Dropsy" class="mw-redirect" title="Dropsy">dropsy</a></li>
<li>1787 – <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Charles" title="Jacques Charles">Jacques Charles</a>: <a href="/wiki/Charles%27s_law" title="Charles&#39;s law">Charles's law</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">ideal gases</a></li>
<li>1789 – <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Lavoisier" title="Antoine Lavoisier">Antoine Lavoisier</a>: law of <a href="/wiki/Conservation_of_mass" title="Conservation of mass">conservation of mass</a>, basis for <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, and the beginning of modern chemistry</li>
<li>1796 – <a href="/wiki/Georges_Cuvier" title="Georges Cuvier">Georges Cuvier</a>: Establishes <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a> as a fact</li>
<li>1796 – <a href="/wiki/Edward_Jenner" title="Edward Jenner">Edward Jenner</a>: <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> historical accounting</li>
<li>1796 – <a href="/wiki/Hanaoka_Seish%C5%AB" title="Hanaoka Seishū">Hanaoka Seishū</a>: develops <a href="/wiki/General_anaesthesia" title="General anaesthesia">general anaesthesia</a></li>
<li>1800 – <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Volta" title="Alessandro Volta">Alessandro Volta</a>: discovers <a href="/wiki/Electrochemical_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrochemical series">electrochemical series</a> and invents the <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battery (electricity)">battery</a></li></ul>
<h2><span id="1800.E2.80.931849"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1800–1849">1800–1849</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=95" title="Edit section: 1800–1849">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1802 – <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Lamarck" title="Jean-Baptiste Lamarck">Jean-Baptiste Lamarck</a>: teleological evolution</li>
<li>1805 – <a href="/wiki/John_Dalton_(scientist)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Dalton (scientist)">John Dalton</a>: <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic Theory">Atomic Theory</a> in (<a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>)</li>
<li>1820 – <a href="/wiki/Hans_Christian_%C3%98rsted" title="Hans Christian Ørsted">Hans Christian Ørsted</a> discovers that a current passed through a wire will deflect the needle of a compass, establishing the deep relationship between electricity and magnetism (<a href="/wiki/Electromagnetism" title="Electromagnetism">electromagnetism</a>).</li>
<li>1820 - <a href="/wiki/Michael_Faraday" title="Michael Faraday">Michael Faraday</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_Stoddart_(instrument_maker)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James Stoddart (instrument maker) (page does not exist)">James Stoddart</a> discover alloying iron with <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">chromium</a> produces a <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a> resistant to oxidising elements (<a href="/wiki/Rust" title="Rust">rust</a>).</li>
<li>1821 – <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Johann_Seebeck" title="Thomas Johann Seebeck">Thomas Johann Seebeck</a> is the first to observe a property of <a href="/wiki/Semiconductors" class="mw-redirect" title="Semiconductors">semiconductors</a></li>
<li>1824 – <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_L%C3%A9onard_Sadi_Carnot" title="Nicolas Léonard Sadi Carnot">Carnot</a>: described the <a href="/wiki/Carnot_cycle" title="Carnot cycle">Carnot cycle</a>, the idealized heat engine</li>
<li>1824 - <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Aspdin" title="Joseph Aspdin">Joseph Aspdin</a> develops <a href="/wiki/Portland_cement" title="Portland cement">Portland cement</a> (<a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">concrete</a>), by heating ground limestone, clay and gypsum, in a kiln.</li>
<li>1827 – <a href="/wiki/Evariste_Galois" class="mw-redirect" title="Evariste Galois">Evariste Galois</a> development of <a href="/wiki/Group_(mathematics)" title="Group (mathematics)">group theory</a></li>
<li>1827 – <a href="/wiki/Georg_Ohm" title="Georg Ohm">Georg Ohm</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ohm%27s_law" title="Ohm&#39;s law">Ohm's law</a> (<a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">Electricity</a>)</li>
<li>1827 – <a href="/wiki/Amedeo_Avogadro" title="Amedeo Avogadro">Amedeo Avogadro</a>: <a href="/wiki/Avogadro%27s_law" title="Avogadro&#39;s law">Avogadro's law</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gas_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas law">Gas law</a>)</li>
<li>1828 – <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_W%C3%B6hler" title="Friedrich Wöhler">Friedrich Wöhler</a> synthesized <a href="/wiki/Urea" title="Urea">urea</a>, refuting <a href="/wiki/Vitalism" title="Vitalism">vitalism</a></li>
<li>1830 – <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Lobachevsky" title="Nikolai Lobachevsky">Nikolai Lobachevsky</a> created <a href="/wiki/Non-Euclidean_geometry" title="Non-Euclidean geometry">Non-Euclidean geometry</a></li>
<li>1831 – <a href="/wiki/Michael_Faraday" title="Michael Faraday">Michael Faraday</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_induction" title="Electromagnetic induction">electromagnetic induction</a></li>
<li>1833 – <a href="/wiki/Anselme_Payen" title="Anselme Payen">Anselme Payen</a> isolates first <a href="/wiki/Enzyme" title="Enzyme">enzyme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diastase" title="Diastase">diastase</a></li>
<li>1837 - <a href="/wiki/Charles_Babbage" title="Charles Babbage">Charles Babbage</a> proposes a design for the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Turing_completeness" title="Turing completeness">Turing complete</a>, general purpose Computer, to be called the <a href="/wiki/Analytical_Engine" title="Analytical Engine">Analytical Engine</a>.</li>
<li>1838 – <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Schleiden" class="mw-redirect" title="Matthias Schleiden">Matthias Schleiden</a>: all plants are made of <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cells</a></li>
<li>1838 – <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Bessel" title="Friedrich Bessel">Friedrich Bessel</a>: first successful measure of <a href="/wiki/Stellar_parallax" title="Stellar parallax">stellar parallax</a> (to star <a href="/wiki/61_Cygni" title="61 Cygni">61 Cygni</a>)</li>
<li>1842 – <a href="/wiki/Christian_Doppler" title="Christian Doppler">Christian Doppler</a>: <a href="/wiki/Doppler_effect" title="Doppler effect">Doppler effect</a></li>
<li>1843 – <a href="/wiki/James_Prescott_Joule" title="James Prescott Joule">James Prescott Joule</a>: Law of <a href="/wiki/Conservation_of_energy" title="Conservation of energy">Conservation of energy</a> (<a href="/wiki/First_law_of_thermodynamics" title="First law of thermodynamics">First law of thermodynamics</a>), also 1847 – <a href="/wiki/Helmholtz" class="mw-redirect" title="Helmholtz">Helmholtz</a>, Conservation of energy</li>
<li>1846 – <a href="/wiki/Johann_Gottfried_Galle" title="Johann Gottfried Galle">Johann Gottfried Galle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Louis_d%27Arrest" title="Heinrich Louis d&#39;Arrest">Heinrich Louis d'Arrest</a>: discovery of <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a></li>
<li>1847 - <a href="/wiki/George_Boole" title="George Boole">George Boole</a>: publishes <i>The Mathematical Analysis of Logic</i>, defining <a href="/wiki/Boolean_algebra" title="Boolean algebra">Boolean algebra</a>; refined in his 1854 <a href="/wiki/The_Laws_of_Thought" title="The Laws of Thought">The Laws of Thought</a>.</li>
<li>1848 – <a href="/wiki/Lord_Kelvin" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Kelvin">Lord Kelvin</a>: <a href="/wiki/Absolute_zero" title="Absolute zero">absolute zero</a></li></ul>
<h2><span id="1850.E2.80.931899"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1850–1899">1850–1899</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=96" title="Edit section: 1850–1899">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1856 - <a href="/wiki/Robert_Forester_Mushet" title="Robert Forester Mushet">Robert Forester Mushet</a> develops a process for the decarbonisation, and re-carbonisation of iron, thorough the addition of a calculated quantity of <a href="/wiki/Spiegeleisen" title="Spiegeleisen">spiegeleisen</a>, to produce cheap, consistently high quality <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>.</li>
<li>1858 – <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Virchow" title="Rudolf Virchow">Rudolf Virchow</a>: <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cells</a> can only arise from pre-existing cells</li>
<li>1859 – <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Wallace" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred Wallace">Alfred Wallace</a>: Theory of <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a> by <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">natural selection</a></li>
<li>1861 – <a href="/wiki/Louis_Pasteur" title="Louis Pasteur">Louis Pasteur</a>: <a href="/wiki/Germ_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Germ theory">Germ theory</a></li>
<li>1861 – <a href="/wiki/John_Tyndall" title="John Tyndall">John Tyndall</a>:  Experiments in Radiant Energy that reinforced the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_effect" title="Greenhouse effect">Greenhouse effect</a></li>
<li>1864 – <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Clerk Maxwell</a>: Theory of <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetism" title="Electromagnetism">electromagnetism</a></li>
<li>1865 – <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Mendel" title="Gregor Mendel">Gregor Mendel</a>: <a href="/wiki/Mendelian_inheritance" title="Mendelian inheritance">Mendel's laws of inheritance</a>, basis for <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a></li>
<li>1865 – <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Clausius" title="Rudolf Clausius">Rudolf Clausius</a>: Definition of <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">entropy</a></li>
<li>1868 - <a href="/wiki/Robert_Forester_Mushet" title="Robert Forester Mushet">Robert Forester Mushet</a> discovers that alloying steel with <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a> produces a harder, more durable alloy.</li>
<li>1869 – <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Mendeleev" title="Dmitri Mendeleev">Dmitri Mendeleev</a>: <a href="/wiki/Periodic_table" title="Periodic table">Periodic table</a></li>
<li>1871 – <a href="/wiki/John_William_Strutt,_3rd_Baron_Rayleigh" title="John William Strutt, 3rd Baron Rayleigh">Lord Rayleigh</a>: <a href="/wiki/Diffuse_sky_radiation" title="Diffuse sky radiation">Diffuse sky radiation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rayleigh_scattering" title="Rayleigh scattering">Rayleigh scattering</a>) explains why sky appears blue</li>
<li>1873 – <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Diderik_van_der_Waals" title="Johannes Diderik van der Waals">Johannes Diderik van der Waals</a>: was one of the first to postulate an intermolecular force: the <a href="/wiki/Van_der_Waals_force" title="Van der Waals force">van der Waals force</a>.</li>
<li>1873 – <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Guthrie" title="Frederick Guthrie">Frederick Guthrie</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Thermionic_emission" title="Thermionic emission">thermionic emission</a>.</li>
<li>1873 – <a href="/wiki/Willoughby_Smith" title="Willoughby Smith">Willoughby Smith</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Photoconductivity" title="Photoconductivity">photoconductivity</a>.</li>
<li>1875 – <a href="/wiki/William_Crookes" title="William Crookes">William Crookes</a> invented the <a href="/wiki/Crookes_tube" title="Crookes tube">Crookes tube</a> and studied <a href="/wiki/Cathode_rays" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathode rays">cathode rays</a></li>
<li>1876 – <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Willard_Gibbs" title="Josiah Willard Gibbs">Josiah Willard Gibbs</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Chemical_thermodynamics" title="Chemical thermodynamics">chemical thermodynamics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Phase_rule" title="Phase rule">phase rule</a></li>
<li>1877 – <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Boltzmann" title="Ludwig Boltzmann">Ludwig Boltzmann</a>: Statistical definition of <a href="/wiki/Entropy_(statistical_thermodynamics)" title="Entropy (statistical thermodynamics)">entropy</a></li>
<li>1880s - <a href="/wiki/John_Hopkinson" title="John Hopkinson">John Hopkinson</a> develops <a href="/wiki/Three-phase" class="mw-redirect" title="Three-phase">three-phase</a> electrical supplies, mathematically proves how multiple AC dynamos can be connected in parallel, improves permanent magnets, and dynamo efficiency, by the addition of tungsten, and describes how temperature effects magnetism (<a href="/wiki/Hopkinson_effect" title="Hopkinson effect">Hopkinson effect</a>).</li>
<li>1880 – <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Curie" title="Pierre Curie">Pierre Curie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Curie" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacques Curie">Jacques Curie</a>: <a href="/wiki/Piezoelectricity" title="Piezoelectricity">Piezoelectricity</a></li>
<li>1884 – <a href="/wiki/Jacobus_Henricus_van_%27t_Hoff" title="Jacobus Henricus van &#39;t Hoff">Jacobus Henricus van 't Hoff</a>: discovered the laws of chemical dynamics and osmotic pressure in solutions (in his work "Études de dynamique chimique").</li>
<li>1887 – <a href="/wiki/Albert_A._Michelson" title="Albert A. Michelson">Albert A. Michelson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_W._Morley" title="Edward W. Morley">Edward W. Morley</a>: <a href="/wiki/Michelson%E2%80%93Morley_experiment" title="Michelson–Morley experiment">Michelson–Morley experiment</a> which showed a lack of evidence for the <a href="/wiki/Aether_(classical_element)" title="Aether (classical element)">aether</a></li>
<li>1888 – <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Reinitzer" title="Friedrich Reinitzer">Friedrich Reinitzer</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Liquid_crystals" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquid crystals">liquid crystals</a></li>
<li>1892 – <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Ivanovsky" title="Dmitri Ivanovsky">Dmitri Ivanovsky</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a></li>
<li>1895 – <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Conrad_R%C3%B6ntgen" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen">Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/X-rays" class="mw-redirect" title="X-rays">x-rays</a></li>
<li>1896 – <a href="/wiki/Henri_Becquerel" title="Henri Becquerel">Henri Becquerel</a> discovers <a href="/wiki/Radioactivity" class="mw-redirect" title="Radioactivity">radioactivity</a></li>
<li>1896 – <a href="/wiki/Svante_Arrhenius" title="Svante Arrhenius">Svante Arrhenius</a> derives the basic principles of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_effect" title="Greenhouse effect">greenhouse effect</a></li>
<li>1897 – <a href="/wiki/J.J._Thomson" class="mw-redirect" title="J.J. Thomson">J.J. Thomson</a> discovers the <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">electron</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cathode_rays" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathode rays">cathode rays</a></li>
<li>1209748393 – <a href="/wiki/Martinus_Beijerinck" title="Martinus Beijerinck">Martinus Beijerinck</a>: concluded that a virus is infectious—replicating in the host—and thus not a mere toxin, and gave it the name "virus"</li>
<li>1898 – <a href="/wiki/J.J._Thomson" class="mw-redirect" title="J.J. Thomson">J.J. Thomson</a> proposed the <a href="/wiki/Plum_pudding_model" title="Plum pudding model">plum pudding model</a> of an atom</li>
<li>1898 - <a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">Marie Curie</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/Radium" title="Radium">radium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polonium" title="Polonium">polonium</a></li></ul>
<h2><span id="1900.E2.80.931949"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1900–1949">1900–1949</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=97" title="Edit section: 1900–1949">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1900 – <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck" title="Max Planck">Max Planck</a>: explains the emission spectrum of a <a href="/wiki/Black_body" title="Black body">black body</a></li>
<li>1905 – <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>: theory of <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>, explanation of <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">Brownian motion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Photoelectric_effect" title="Photoelectric effect">photoelectric effect</a></li>
<li>1906 – <a href="/wiki/Walther_Nernst" title="Walther Nernst">Walther Nernst</a>: <a href="/wiki/Third_law_of_thermodynamics" title="Third law of thermodynamics">Third law of thermodynamics</a></li>
<li>1907 – <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Bertheim" title="Alfred Bertheim">Alfred Bertheim</a>: <a href="/wiki/Arsphenamine" title="Arsphenamine">Arsphenamine</a>, the first modern <a href="/wiki/Antimicrobial_chemotherapy" title="Antimicrobial chemotherapy">chemotherapeutic agent</a></li>
<li>1909 – <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Haber" title="Fritz Haber">Fritz Haber</a>: <a href="/wiki/Haber_Process" class="mw-redirect" title="Haber Process">Haber Process</a> for industrial production of ammonia</li>
<li>1909 – <a href="/wiki/Robert_Andrews_Millikan" title="Robert Andrews Millikan">Robert Andrews Millikan</a>: conducts the <a href="/wiki/Oil_drop_experiment" title="Oil drop experiment">oil drop experiment</a> and determines the charge on an electron</li>
<li>1910 – <a href="/wiki/Williamina_Paton_Stevens_Fleming" class="mw-redirect" title="Williamina Paton Stevens Fleming">Williamina Fleming</a>: the first <a href="/wiki/White_dwarf" title="White dwarf">white dwarf</a>, <a href="/wiki/40_Eridani_B" class="mw-redirect" title="40 Eridani B">40 Eridani B</a></li>
<li>1911 – <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a>: <a href="/wiki/Atomic_nucleus" title="Atomic nucleus">Atomic nucleus</a></li>
<li>1911 – <a href="/wiki/Heike_Kamerlingh_Onnes" title="Heike Kamerlingh Onnes">Heike Kamerlingh Onnes</a>: <a href="/wiki/Superconductivity" title="Superconductivity">Superconductivity</a></li>
<li>1912 – <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Wegener" title="Alfred Wegener">Alfred Wegener</a>: <a href="/wiki/Continental_drift" title="Continental drift">Continental drift</a></li>
<li>1912 – <a href="/wiki/Max_von_Laue" title="Max von Laue">Max von Laue</a>&#160;: <a href="/wiki/X-ray_diffraction" class="mw-redirect" title="X-ray diffraction">x-ray diffraction</a></li>
<li>1912 – <a href="/wiki/Vesto_Slipher" class="mw-redirect" title="Vesto Slipher">Vesto Slipher</a>&#160;: <a href="/wiki/Galaxy" title="Galaxy">galactic</a> <a href="/wiki/Redshift" title="Redshift">redshifts</a></li>
<li>1912 – <a href="/wiki/Henrietta_Swan_Leavitt" title="Henrietta Swan Leavitt">Henrietta Swan Leavitt</a>: <a href="/wiki/Cepheid_variable" title="Cepheid variable">Cepheid variable</a> <a href="/wiki/Period-luminosity_relation" title="Period-luminosity relation">period-luminosity relation</a></li>
<li>1913 – <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moseley" title="Henry Moseley">Henry Moseley</a>: defined <a href="/wiki/Atomic_number" title="Atomic number">atomic number</a></li>
<li>1913 – <a href="/wiki/Niels_Bohr" title="Niels Bohr">Niels Bohr</a>: <a href="/wiki/Bohr_model" title="Bohr model">Model of the atom</a></li>
<li>1915 – <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>: theory of <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a> – also <a href="/wiki/David_Hilbert" title="David Hilbert">David Hilbert</a></li>
<li>1915 – <a href="/wiki/Karl_Schwarzschild" title="Karl Schwarzschild">Karl Schwarzschild</a>: discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Schwarzschild_radius" title="Schwarzschild radius">Schwarzschild radius</a> leading to the identification of <a href="/wiki/Black_holes" class="mw-redirect" title="Black holes">black holes</a></li>
<li>1918 – <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Noether" title="Emmy Noether">Emmy Noether</a>: <a href="/wiki/Noether%27s_theorem" title="Noether&#39;s theorem">Noether's theorem</a> – conditions under which the conservation laws are valid</li>
<li>1920 – <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Eddington" title="Arthur Eddington">Arthur Eddington</a>: <a href="/wiki/Stellar_nucleosynthesis" title="Stellar nucleosynthesis">Stellar nucleosynthesis</a></li>
<li>1922 – <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Banting" title="Frederick Banting">Frederick Banting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Herbert_Best" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Herbert Best">Charles Best</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Collip" title="James Collip">James Collip</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_James_Rickard_Macleod" class="mw-redirect" title="John James Rickard Macleod">John Macleod</a>: isolation and production of <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a> to control diabetes</li>
<li>1924 – <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Pauli" title="Wolfgang Pauli">Wolfgang Pauli</a>: quantum <a href="/wiki/Pauli_exclusion_principle" title="Pauli exclusion principle">Pauli exclusion principle</a></li>
<li>1924 – <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hubble" title="Edwin Hubble">Edwin Hubble</a>: the discovery that the <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">Milky Way</a> is just one of many galaxies</li>
<li>1925 – <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Schr%C3%B6dinger" title="Erwin Schrödinger">Erwin Schrödinger</a>: <a href="/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger_equation" title="Schrödinger equation">Schrödinger equation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">Quantum mechanics</a>)</li>
<li>1925 – <a href="/wiki/Cecilia_Payne-Gaposchkin" title="Cecilia Payne-Gaposchkin">Cecilia Payne-Gaposchkin</a>: Discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Metallicity" title="Metallicity">composition of the Sun</a> and that <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> is the most abundant element in the Universe</li>
<li>1927 – <a href="/wiki/Werner_Heisenberg" title="Werner Heisenberg">Werner Heisenberg</a>: <a href="/wiki/Uncertainty_principle" title="Uncertainty principle">Uncertainty principle</a> (<a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">Quantum mechanics</a>)</li>
<li>1927 – <a href="/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre" title="Georges Lemaître">Georges Lemaître</a>: Theory of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a></li>
<li>1928 – <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dirac" title="Paul Dirac">Paul Dirac</a>: <a href="/wiki/Dirac_equation" title="Dirac equation">Dirac equation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">Quantum mechanics</a>)</li>
<li>1929 – <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hubble" title="Edwin Hubble">Edwin Hubble</a>: <a href="/wiki/Hubble%27s_law" title="Hubble&#39;s law">Hubble's law</a> of the expanding <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a></li>
<li>1929 – <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Fleming" title="Alexander Fleming">Alexander Fleming</a>: <a href="/wiki/Benzylpenicillin" title="Benzylpenicillin">Penicillin</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Beta-lactam_antibiotic" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta-lactam antibiotic">beta-lactam antibiotic</a></li>
<li>1929 – <a href="/wiki/Lars_Onsager" title="Lars Onsager">Lars Onsager</a>'s reciprocal relations, a potential fourth <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_thermodynamics" title="Laws of thermodynamics">law of thermodynamics</a></li>
<li>1930 – <a href="/wiki/Subrahmanyan_Chandrasekhar" title="Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar">Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar</a> discovers his <a href="/wiki/Chandrasekhar_limit" title="Chandrasekhar limit">eponymous limit</a> of the maximum mass of a <a href="/wiki/White_dwarf" title="White dwarf">white dwarf</a> star</li>
<li>1931 – <a href="/wiki/Kurt_G%C3%B6del" title="Kurt Gödel">Kurt Gödel</a>: <a href="/wiki/Incompleteness_theorems" class="mw-redirect" title="Incompleteness theorems">incompleteness theorems</a> prove formal axiomatic systems are incomplete</li>
<li>1932 – <a href="/wiki/James_Chadwick" title="James Chadwick">James Chadwick</a>: Discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">neutron</a></li>
<li>1932 – <a href="/wiki/Karl_Guthe_Jansky" title="Karl Guthe Jansky">Karl Guthe Jansky</a> discovers the first <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_radio_source" title="Astronomical radio source">astronomical radio source</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sagittarius_A" title="Sagittarius A">Sagittarius A</a></li>
<li>1932 – <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Walton" title="Ernest Walton">Ernest Walton</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Cockcroft" title="John Cockcroft">John Cockcroft</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fission" title="Nuclear fission">Nuclear fission</a> by proton bombardment</li>
<li>1934 – <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Fermi" title="Enrico Fermi">Enrico Fermi</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fission" title="Nuclear fission">Nuclear fission</a> by neutron irradiation</li>
<li>1934 – <a href="/wiki/Clive_McCay" title="Clive McCay">Clive McCay</a>: <a href="/wiki/Calorie_restriction" title="Calorie restriction">Calorie restriction</a> extends the maximum lifespan of another <a href="/wiki/James_Watson" title="James Watson">species</a></li>
<li>1938 – <a href="/wiki/Otto_Hahn" title="Otto Hahn">Otto Hahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lise_Meitner" title="Lise Meitner">Lise Meitner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Strassmann" title="Fritz Strassmann">Fritz Strassmann</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fission" title="Nuclear fission">Nuclear fission</a> of heavy nuclei</li>
<li>1938 – <a href="/wiki/Isidor_Rabi" class="mw-redirect" title="Isidor Rabi">Isidor Rabi</a>: <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_magnetic_resonance" title="Nuclear magnetic resonance">Nuclear magnetic resonance</a></li>
<li>1943 – <a href="/wiki/Oswald_Avery" title="Oswald Avery">Oswald Avery</a> proves that <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> is the genetic material of the <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosome</a></li>
<li>1945 – <a href="/wiki/Howard_Florey" title="Howard Florey">Howard Florey</a> Mass production of <a href="/wiki/Penicillin" title="Penicillin">penicillin</a></li>
<li>1947 – <a href="/wiki/William_Shockley" title="William Shockley">William Shockley</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Bardeen" title="John Bardeen">John Bardeen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Brattain" class="mw-redirect" title="Walter Brattain">Walter Brattain</a> invent the first transistor</li>
<li>1948 – <a href="/wiki/Claude_Elwood_Shannon" class="mw-redirect" title="Claude Elwood Shannon">Claude Elwood Shannon</a>: 'A mathematical theory of communication' a seminal paper in <a href="/wiki/Information_theory" title="Information theory">Information theory</a>.</li>
<li>1948 – <a href="/wiki/Richard_Feynman" title="Richard Feynman">Richard Feynman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julian_Schwinger" title="Julian Schwinger">Julian Schwinger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sin-Itiro_Tomonaga" class="mw-redirect" title="Sin-Itiro Tomonaga">Sin-Itiro Tomonaga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freeman_Dyson" title="Freeman Dyson">Freeman Dyson</a>: <a href="/wiki/Quantum_electrodynamics" title="Quantum electrodynamics">Quantum electrodynamics</a></li></ul>
<h2><span id="1950.E2.80.931999"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1950–1999">1950–1999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=98" title="Edit section: 1950–1999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>1951 – <a href="/wiki/George_Otto_Gey" title="George Otto Gey">George Otto Gey</a> propagates first cancer cell line, <a href="/wiki/HeLa" title="HeLa">HeLa</a></li>
<li>1952 – <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Salk" title="Jonas Salk">Jonas Salk</a>: developed and tested first <a href="/wiki/Polio_vaccine" title="Polio vaccine">polio vaccine</a></li>
<li>1952 – <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Miller" title="Stanley Miller">Stanley Miller</a>: demonstrated that the building blocks of life could arise from primeval soup in the conditions present during early earth (<a href="/wiki/Miller%E2%80%93Urey_experiment" title="Miller–Urey experiment">Miller-Urey experiment</a>)</li>
<li>1952 – <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Sanger" title="Frederick Sanger">Frederick Sanger</a>: demonstrated that <a href="/wiki/Proteins" class="mw-redirect" title="Proteins">proteins</a> are sequences of <a href="/wiki/Amino_acids" class="mw-redirect" title="Amino acids">amino acids</a></li>
<li>1953 – <a href="/wiki/James_Watson" title="James Watson">James Watson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick" title="Francis Crick">Francis Crick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Wilkins" title="Maurice Wilkins">Maurice Wilkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rosalind_Franklin" title="Rosalind Franklin">Rosalind Franklin</a>: helical structure of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a>, basis for <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a></li>
<li>1957 - <a href="/wiki/Chien_Shiung_Wu" class="mw-redirect" title="Chien Shiung Wu">Chien Shiung Wu</a>: demonstrated that <a href="/wiki/Parity_(physics)" title="Parity (physics)">parity</a>, and thus <a href="/wiki/Charge_conjugation" class="mw-redirect" title="Charge conjugation">charge conjugation</a> and <a href="/wiki/T-symmetry" title="T-symmetry">time-reversals</a>, are <a href="/wiki/Cp_violation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cp violation">violated</a> for <a href="/wiki/Weak_interaction" title="Weak interaction">weak interactions</a></li>
<li>1962 – <a href="/wiki/Riccardo_Giacconi" title="Riccardo Giacconi">Riccardo Giacconi</a> and his team discover the first <a href="/wiki/X-ray_astronomy" title="X-ray astronomy">cosmic x-ray source</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scorpius_X-1" title="Scorpius X-1">Scorpius X-1</a></li>
<li>1963 – <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Morley" title="Lawrence Morley">Lawrence Morley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_Vine" class="mw-redirect" title="Fred Vine">Fred Vine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drummond_Matthews" title="Drummond Matthews">Drummond Matthews</a>:  Paleomagnetic stripes in ocean crust as evidence of <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">plate tectonics</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vine%E2%80%93Matthews%E2%80%93Morley_hypothesis" title="Vine–Matthews–Morley hypothesis">Vine–Matthews–Morley hypothesis</a>).</li>
<li>1964 – <a href="/wiki/Murray_Gell-Mann" title="Murray Gell-Mann">Murray Gell-Mann</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Zweig" title="George Zweig">George Zweig</a>: postulates <a href="/wiki/Quarks" class="mw-redirect" title="Quarks">quarks</a>, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Standard_model" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard model">standard model</a></li>
<li>1964 – <a href="/wiki/Arno_Penzias" class="mw-redirect" title="Arno Penzias">Arno Penzias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Woodrow_Wilson" title="Robert Woodrow Wilson">Robert Woodrow Wilson</a>: detection of <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background_radiation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cosmic microwave background radiation">CMBR</a> providing experimental evidence for the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a></li>
<li>1965 – <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Hayflick" title="Leonard Hayflick">Leonard Hayflick</a>: normal cells divide only a certain number of times: the <a href="/wiki/Hayflick_limit" title="Hayflick limit">Hayflick limit</a></li>
<li>1967 – <a href="/wiki/Jocelyn_Bell_Burnell" title="Jocelyn Bell Burnell">Jocelyn Bell Burnell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antony_Hewish" title="Antony Hewish">Antony Hewish</a> discover first <a href="/wiki/Pulsar" title="Pulsar">pulsar</a></li>
<li>1967 – <a href="/wiki/Vela_(satellite)" title="Vela (satellite)">Vela</a> nuclear test detection satellites discover the first <a href="/wiki/Gamma-ray_burst" title="Gamma-ray burst">gamma-ray burst</a></li>
<li>1970 - <a href="/wiki/James_H._Ellis" title="James H. Ellis">James H. Ellis</a> proposed the possibility of "non-secret encryption", more commonly termed <a href="/wiki/Public-key_cryptography" title="Public-key cryptography">public-key cryptography</a>, a concept that would be implemented by his <a href="/wiki/GCHQ" title="GCHQ">GCHQ</a> colleague <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Cocks" title="Clifford Cocks">Clifford Cocks</a> in 1973, in what would become known as the RSA algorithm, with key exchange added by a third colleague <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_J._Williamson" title="Malcolm J. Williamson">Malcolm J. Williamson</a>, in 1975.</li>
<li>1971 – <a href="/wiki/Place_cells" class="mw-redirect" title="Place cells">Place cells</a> in the brain are discovered by <a href="/wiki/John_O%27Keefe_(neuroscientist)" title="John O&#39;Keefe (neuroscientist)">John O'Keefe</a></li>
<li>1974 – <a href="/wiki/Russell_Alan_Hulse" title="Russell Alan Hulse">Russell Alan Hulse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Hooton_Taylor,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Hooton Taylor, Jr.">Joseph Hooton Taylor, Jr.</a> discover indirect evidence for <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_wave" title="Gravitational wave">gravitational wave radiation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hulse%E2%80%93Taylor_binary" title="Hulse–Taylor binary">Hulse–Taylor binary</a></li>
<li>1977 – <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Sanger" title="Frederick Sanger">Frederick Sanger</a> sequences the first DNA genome of an organism using <a href="/wiki/Sanger_sequencing" title="Sanger sequencing">Sanger sequencing</a></li>
<li>1980 – <a href="/wiki/Klaus_von_Klitzing" title="Klaus von Klitzing">Klaus von Klitzing</a> discovered the <a href="/wiki/Quantum_Hall_effect" title="Quantum Hall effect">quantum Hall effect</a></li>
<li>1982 – <a href="/wiki/Donald_C._Backer" title="Donald C. Backer">Donald C. Backer</a> et al. discover the first <a href="/wiki/Millisecond_pulsar" title="Millisecond pulsar">millisecond pulsar</a></li>
<li>1983 – <a href="/wiki/Kary_Mullis" title="Kary Mullis">Kary Mullis</a> invents the <a href="/wiki/Polymerase_chain_reaction" title="Polymerase chain reaction">polymerase chain reaction</a>, a key discovery in <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">molecular biology</a></li>
<li>1986 – <a href="/wiki/Karl_Alexander_M%C3%BCller" class="mw-redirect" title="Karl Alexander Müller">Karl Müller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Bednorz" class="mw-redirect" title="Johannes Bednorz">Johannes Bednorz</a>: Discovery of <a href="/wiki/High-temperature_superconductivity" title="High-temperature superconductivity">High-temperature superconductivity</a></li>
<li>1988 –  <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bart_van_Wees&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bart van Wees (page does not exist)">Bart van Wees</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bart_van_Wees" class="extiw" title="nl:Bart van Wees">nl</a>&#93;</span> and colleagues at TU Deflt and Philips Research discovered the <a href="/wiki/Conductance_quantum" title="Conductance quantum">quantized conductance</a> in a two-dimensional electron gas.</li>
<li>1992 – <a href="/wiki/Aleksander_Wolszczan" title="Aleksander Wolszczan">Aleksander Wolszczan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Frail" title="Dale Frail">Dale Frail</a> observe the first pulsar planets (this was the first confirmed discovery of planets outside the Solar System)</li>
<li>1994 – <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Wiles" title="Andrew Wiles">Andrew Wiles</a> proves <a href="/wiki/Fermat%27s_Last_Theorem" title="Fermat&#39;s Last Theorem">Fermat's Last Theorem</a></li>
<li>1995 – <a href="/wiki/Michel_Mayor" title="Michel Mayor">Michel Mayor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Didier_Queloz" class="mw-redirect" title="Didier Queloz">Didier Queloz</a> definitively observe the first <a href="/wiki/Extrasolar_planet" class="mw-redirect" title="Extrasolar planet">extrasolar planet</a> around a <a href="/wiki/Main_sequence_star" class="mw-redirect" title="Main sequence star">main sequence star</a></li>
<li>1995 – <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cornell" class="mw-redirect" title="Eric Cornell">Eric Cornell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Wieman" title="Carl Wieman">Carl Wieman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Ketterle" title="Wolfgang Ketterle">Wolfgang Ketterle</a> attained the first <a href="/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_condensate" title="Bose–Einstein condensate">Bose-Einstein Condensate</a> with atomic gases, so called fifth state of matter at an extremely low temperature.</li>
<li>1996 – <a href="/wiki/Roslin_Institute" title="Roslin Institute">Roslin Institute</a>: <a href="/wiki/Dolly_the_sheep" class="mw-redirect" title="Dolly the sheep">Dolly the sheep</a> was cloned.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1997 – <a href="/wiki/Collider_Detector_at_Fermilab" title="Collider Detector at Fermilab">CDF</a> and <a href="/wiki/D0_experiment" class="mw-redirect" title="D0 experiment">DØ</a> experiments at <a href="/wiki/Fermilab" title="Fermilab">Fermilab</a>: <a href="/wiki/Top_quark" title="Top quark">Top quark</a>.</li>
<li>1998 – <a href="/wiki/Supernova_Cosmology_Project" title="Supernova Cosmology Project">Supernova Cosmology Project</a> and the <a href="/wiki/High-Z_Supernova_Search_Team" title="High-Z Supernova Search Team">High-Z Supernova Search Team</a>: discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Accelerating_universe" class="mw-redirect" title="Accelerating universe">accelerated expansion of the Universe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">dark energy</a></li>
<li>2000 – The <a href="/wiki/Tau_neutrino" title="Tau neutrino">Tau neutrino</a> is discovered by the <a href="/wiki/DONUT" title="DONUT">DONUT collaboration</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=99" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_years_in_science#2000s" title="List of years in science">List of years in science §&#160;2000s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_of_the_Year#Breakthrough_of_the_Year" title="Breakthrough of the Year">Breakthrough of the Year §&#160;Breakthrough of the Year</a></div>
<ul><li>2001 – The first draft of the <a href="/wiki/Human_Genome_Project" title="Human Genome Project">Human Genome Project</a> is published.</li>
<li>2003 – <a href="/wiki/Grigori_Perelman" title="Grigori Perelman">Grigori Perelman</a> presents proof of the <a href="/wiki/Poincar%C3%A9_Conjecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Poincaré Conjecture">Poincaré Conjecture</a>.</li>
<li>2004 – <a href="/wiki/Andre_Geim" title="Andre Geim">Andre Geim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Novoselov" title="Konstantin Novoselov">Konstantin Novoselov</a> isolated <a href="/wiki/Graphene" title="Graphene">graphene</a>, a monolayer of carbon atoms, and studied its quantum electrical properties.</li>
<li>2005 – <a href="/wiki/Grid_cells" class="mw-redirect" title="Grid cells">Grid cells</a> in the brain are discovered by <a href="/wiki/Edvard_Moser" title="Edvard Moser">Edvard Moser</a> and <a href="/wiki/May-Britt_Moser" title="May-Britt Moser">May-Britt Moser</a>.</li>
<li>2010 – The first self-replicating, synthetic bacterial cells are constructed.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2010 – The <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal_Genome_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Neanderthal Genome Project">Neanderthal Genome Project</a> presented preliminary genetic evidence that interbreeding did likely take place and that a small but significant portion of Neanderthal admixture is present in modern non-African populations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>2012 – <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a> is discovered at <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> (confirmed to 99.999% certainty)</li>
<li>2012 – <a href="/wiki/Photonic_molecule" title="Photonic molecule">Photonic molecules</a> are discovered at <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a></li>
<li>2014 – <a href="/wiki/Exotic_hadron" title="Exotic hadron">Exotic hadrons</a> are discovered at the LHCb</li>
<li>2014 – <a href="/wiki/Photonic_metamaterial" title="Photonic metamaterial">Photonic metamaterials</a> are discovered to make <a href="/wiki/Passive_daytime_radiative_cooling" title="Passive daytime radiative cooling">passive daytime radiative cooling</a> possible by Raman et al.<sup id="cite_ref-:35_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:35-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:372_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:372-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2016 – The <a href="/wiki/LIGO" title="LIGO">LIGO</a> team detected <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_waves" class="mw-redirect" title="Gravitational waves">gravitational waves</a> from a <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_merger" class="mw-redirect" title="Black hole merger">black hole merger</a></li>
<li>2017 – Gravitational wave signal <a href="/wiki/GW170817" title="GW170817">GW170817</a> was observed by the <a href="/wiki/LIGO" title="LIGO">LIGO</a>/<a href="/wiki/Virgo_interferometer" title="Virgo interferometer">Virgo</a> collaboration. This was the first instance of a gravitational wave event that was observed to have a simultaneous electromagnetic signal when space telescopes like <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble</a> observed lights coming from the event, thereby marking a significant breakthrough for multi-messenger astronomy.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>2019 – The <a href="/wiki/Black_hole#Observational_evidence" title="Black hole">first ever image of a black hole was captured</a>, using eight different telescopes taking simultaneous pictures, timed with extremely precise atomic clocks.</li>
<li>2020 – <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> and <a href="/wiki/SOFIA" class="mw-redirect" title="SOFIA">SOFIA</a> (Stratospheric Observatory for Infrared Astronomy) discovered about 12oz of surface water in one of the moon's largest visible craters.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2021_in_science" title="2021 in science">2021 in science</a> and <a href="/wiki/2022_in_science" title="2022 in science">2022 in science</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_scientific_discoveries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=100" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-ed-cam-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ed-cam_40-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ed-cam_40-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ed-cam_40-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"/><cite id="CITEREFEdwards2013" class="citation cs2">Edwards, A. <li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"/><cite id="CITEREFAmulya_Kumar_Bag1966" class="citation journal cs1">Amulya Kumar Bag (6 January 1966). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://insa.nic.in/writereaddata/UpLoadedFiles/IJHS/Vol01_1_8_AKBag.pdf">"Binomial theorem in Ancient India"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Indian J.
